      <p><b>East Timor</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/-<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">iː</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ɔːr/: 'ar' in 'war'">ɔːr</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-East_Timor.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3d/En-us-East_Timor.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-East Timor.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>) or <b>Timor-Leste</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ɔːr/: 'ar' in 'war'">ɔːr</span></span><span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ɛ/: 'e' in 'dress'">ɛ</span><span title="/ʃ/: 'sh' in 'shy'">ʃ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">eɪ</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Tetum_language" title="Tetum language">Tetum</a>: <i lang="tet">Timór Lorosa'e</i>), officially the <b>Democratic Republic of Timor-Leste</b><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <i lang="pt">República Democrática de Timor-Leste</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-ConstitPORT_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ConstitPORT-12">[12]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tetum_language" title="Tetum language">Tetum</a>: <i lang="tet">Repúblika Demokrátika Timór-Leste</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-ConstitTETUM_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ConstitTETUM-13">[13]</a></sup> is an <a href="/wiki/Island_country" title="Island country">island country</a> in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-14">[14]</a></sup> It comprises the eastern half of the island of <a href="/wiki/Timor" title="Timor">Timor</a>, the nearby islands of <a href="/wiki/Atauro_Island" title="Atauro Island">Atauro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jaco_Island" title="Jaco Island">Jaco</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Oecusse" title="Oecusse">Oecusse</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Enclave_and_exclave" title="Enclave and exclave"> exclave</a> on the northwestern side of the island surrounded by <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesian</a> <a href="/wiki/West_Timor" title="West Timor">West Timor</a>. <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> is the country's southern neighbour, separated by the <a href="/wiki/Timor_Sea" title="Timor Sea">Timor Sea</a>. The country's size is about 15,007 square kilometres (5,794&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-auto_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-7">[7]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>East Timor was colonised by <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> in the 16th century and was known as <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Timor" title="Portuguese Timor">Portuguese Timor</a> until 28 November 1975, when the <a href="/wiki/Fretilin" title="Fretilin">Revolutionary Front for an Independent East Timor</a> (Fretilin) declared the territory's independence. Nine days later, it was <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_invasion_of_East_Timor" title="Indonesian invasion of East Timor">invaded</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_occupation_of_East_Timor" title="Indonesian occupation of East Timor">occupied</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_National_Armed_Forces" title="Indonesian National Armed Forces">Indonesian military</a>; it was declared Indonesia's <a href="/wiki/East_Timor_(Indonesian_province)" title="East Timor (Indonesian province)">27th province</a> the following year. The Indonesian occupation of East Timor was characterised by a highly violent, decades-long conflict between separatist groups (especially Fretilin) and the Indonesian military. </p>
      <p>In 1999, following the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>-sponsored act of <a href="/wiki/Self-determination" title="Self-determination">self-determination</a>, Indonesia relinquished control of the territory. As <i>Timor-Leste</i>, it became the first new <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> of the 21st century on 20 May 2002 and joined the United Nations<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Community of Portuguese Language Countries</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> In 2011, East Timor announced its <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_East_Timor_to_the_Association_of_Southeast_Asian_Nations" class="mw-redirect" title="Accession of East Timor to the Association of Southeast Asian Nations">intention to become the eleventh member</a> of the <a href="/wiki/ASEAN" title="ASEAN">Association of Southeast Asian Nations</a> (ASEAN).<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> It is one of only two predominantly <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Asia" title="Christianity in Asia">Christian</a> nations in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>, the other being the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> as well as the only country of <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> to be located completely in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">Southern Hemisphere</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading">

        <h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span>
       </div> 
       <ul> 
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Etymology"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Etymology</span></a></li> 
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a> 
         <ul> 
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3"><a href="#Prehistory"><span class="tocnumber">2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Prehistory</span></a></li> 
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4"><a href="#Classical_era"><span class="tocnumber">2.2</span> <span class="toctext">Classical era</span></a></li> 
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5"><a href="#Colonial_era"><span class="tocnumber">2.3</span> <span class="toctext">Colonial era</span></a> 
           <ul> 
            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-6"><a href="#Portuguese_period_(1769–1975)"><span class="tocnumber">2.3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Portuguese period (1769–1975)</span></a></li>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Timor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>"Timor" is derived from <i>timur</i>, the word for "east" in <a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">Malay</a>, which became recorded as <i>Timor</i> in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>, thus resulting in the <a href="/wiki/Tautological_place_name" class="mw-redirect" title="Tautological place name">tautological toponym</a> meaning "East East": In Portuguese <i>Timor-Leste</i> (<i>Leste</i> being the word for "east"); in <a href="/wiki/Tetum" class="mw-redirect" title="Tetum">Tetum</a> <i>Timór Lorosa'e</i> (<i>Lorosa'e</i> being the word for "east" (literally "rising sun")). In Indonesian, the country is called <i>Timor Timur</i>, thereby using the Portuguese name for the island followed by the word for "east", as adjectives in Indonesian are put after the noun. </p>
      <p>The official names under the Constitution are Democratic Republic of Timor-Leste in English,<sup id="cite_ref-ConstitENG_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ConstitENG-20">[20]</a></sup> República Democrática de Timor-Leste in Portuguese,<sup id="cite_ref-ConstitPORT_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ConstitPORT-12">[12]</a></sup> and Repúblika Demokrátika Timór-Leste in Tetum.<sup id="cite_ref-ConstitTETUM_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ConstitTETUM-13">[13]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/International_Organization_for_Standardization" title="International Organization for Standardization">International Organization for Standardization</a> (ISO) <a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-1" title="ISO 3166-1">official short form</a> in English and all other languages is <i>Timor-Leste</i> (codes: TLS &amp; TL), which has been adopted by the United Nations,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> the European Union,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup>and the national standards organisations of France (<a href="/wiki/AFNOR" title="AFNOR">AFNOR</a>), the United States (<a href="/wiki/ANSI" class="mw-redirect" title="ANSI">ANSI</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> United Kingdom (<a href="/wiki/BSI_Group" title="BSI Group">BSI</a>), <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> (<a href="/wiki/DIN" class="mw-redirect" title="DIN">DIN</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> (<a href="/wiki/Swedish_Standards_Institute" class="mw-redirect" title="Swedish Standards Institute">SIS</a>), all diplomatic missions to the country by protocol and the CIA World Factbook.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Timor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_East_Timor" title="History of East Timor">History of East Timor</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Timor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Prehistory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Cultural remains at <a href="/wiki/Jerimalai" class="mw-redirect" title="Jerimalai">Jerimalai</a> on the eastern tip of East Timor have been dated to 42,000 years ago, making that location one of the oldest known sites of modern human activity in <a href="/wiki/Maritime_Southeast_Asia" title="Maritime Southeast Asia">Maritime Southeast Asia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Descendants of at least three waves of migration are believed still to live in East Timor. The first is described by anthropologists as people of the <a href="/wiki/Vedda_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Vedda people">Veddo</a>-<a href="/wiki/Australoid" class="mw-redirect" title="Australoid">Australoid</a> type. Around 3000 BC, a second migration brought <a href="/wiki/Melanesians" title="Melanesians">Melanesians</a>. The earlier Veddo-Australoid peoples withdrew at this time to the mountainous interior. Finally, proto-Malays arrived from south <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> and north <a href="/wiki/Indochina" class="mw-redirect" title="Indochina">Indochina</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Hakka traders are among those descended from this final group.<sup id="cite_ref-TL_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TL-27">[27]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Timorese origin myths tell of ancestors who sailed around the eastern end of Timor arriving on land in the south. Some stories recount Timorese ancestors journeying from the <a href="/wiki/Malay_Peninsula" title="Malay Peninsula">Malay Peninsula</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Minangkabau_people" title="Minangkabau people">Minangkabau</a> highlands of <a href="/wiki/Sumatra" title="Sumatra">Sumatra</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Taylor_2003_378_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Taylor_2003_378-28">[28]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_peoples" title="Austronesian peoples">Austronesians</a> migrated to Timor, and are thought to be associated with the development of agriculture on the island.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Classical_era">Classical era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Timor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Classical era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Greater_India" title="Greater India">Greater India</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Pre-colonial_Timor_(pre-1515)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pre-colonial Timor (pre-1515)">Before European colonialism</a>, Timor was included in Indonesian/Malaysian, Chinese, and Indian trading networks, and in the 14th century was an exporter of aromatic <a href="/wiki/Sandalwood" title="Sandalwood">sandalwood</a>, slaves, honey, and wax. From the 1500s, the Timorese people had military ties with the <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%A7%C3%B5es" class="mw-redirect" title="Luções">Luções</a> of present-day northern <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> It was the relative abundance of sandalwood on Timor that attracted European explorers to the island in the early 16th century.<sup id="cite_ref-leibosteven_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leibosteven-31">[31]</a></sup> At around that time, European explorers reported that the island had a number of small chiefdoms or princedoms.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_era">Colonial era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Timor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Colonial era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Penfui" title="Battle of Penfui">Battle of Penfui</a>
      </div> 
      <h4><span id="Portuguese_period_.281769.E2.80.931975.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Portuguese_period_(1769–1975)">Portuguese period (1769–1975)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Timor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Portuguese period (1769–1975)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>The Portuguese established outposts in <a href="/wiki/Timor" title="Timor">Timor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maluku_Islands" title="Maluku Islands">Maluku</a>. Effective European occupation of a small part of present-day East Timor began in 1769 when the city of <a href="/wiki/Dili" title="Dili">Dili</a> was founded and the colony of <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Timor" title="Portuguese Timor">Portuguese Timor</a> declared.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> A definitive <a href="/wiki/East_Timor%E2%80%93Indonesia_border" title="East Timor–Indonesia border">border</a> between the Dutch-colonised western half of the island and the Portuguese-colonised eastern half was established by the <a href="/wiki/Permanent_Court_of_Arbitration" title="Permanent Court of Arbitration">Permanent Court of Arbitration</a> of 1914,<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> and it remains the international boundary between the successor states Indonesia and East Timor, respectively. For the Portuguese, East Timor remained little more than a neglected trading post until the late nineteenth century, with minimal investment in infrastructure, health, and education. Sandalwood continued to be the main export crop with coffee exports becoming significant in the mid-nineteenth century. </p>
      <p>At the beginning of the twentieth century, a faltering home economy prompted the Portuguese to extract greater wealth from its colonies, which was met with East Timorese resistance.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-34">[34]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Portuguese Timor had been a place of exile for political and social opponents deported from the metropolis since the late nineteenth century. Among them a large proportion were members of the anarchist and anarcho-syndicalist movement, which until the Second World War was the most influential of the left-wing movements in Portugal. The main waves of deportations to Timor were in 1896, 1927, and 1931. Some of the activists continued their resistance even in exile. After World War II, the remaining exiles were pardoned and allowed to return.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, first the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allies</a> and later the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Japanese</a> occupied Dili, and the mountainous interior of the colony became the scene of a <a href="/wiki/Guerrilla_warfare" title="Guerrilla warfare">guerrilla</a> campaign, known as the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Timor_(1942%E2%80%9343)" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Timor (1942–43)">Battle of Timor</a>. Waged by East Timorese volunteers and Allied forces against the Japanese, the struggle resulted in the deaths of between 40,000 and 70,000 East Timorese civilians.<sup id="cite_ref-ASNCE_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ASNCE-36">[36]</a></sup> The Japanese eventually drove the last of the Australian and Allied forces out. However, Portuguese control was reinstated after the Japanese surrender at the end of World War II. </p>
      <p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Carnation_Revolution" title="Carnation Revolution">1974 Portuguese revolution</a>, Portugal effectively abandoned its colony in Timor and civil war between East Timorese political parties broke out in 1975. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Fretilin" title="Fretilin">The Revolutionary Front for an Independent East Timor (Fretilin)</a> resisted a <a href="/wiki/Timorese_Democratic_Union" title="Timorese Democratic Union">Timorese Democratic Union</a> (UDT) coup attempt in August 1975,<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/East_Timorese_declaration_of_independence" class="mw-redirect" title="East Timorese declaration of independence">unilaterally declared independence</a> on 28 November 1975. Fearing a communist state within the Indonesian archipelago, the Indonesian military launched an <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_invasion_of_East_Timor" title="Indonesian invasion of East Timor">invasion of East Timor</a> in December 1975.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Indonesia declared <a href="/wiki/East_Timor_(Indonesian_province)" title="East Timor (Indonesian province)">East Timor its 27th province</a> on 17 July 1976.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> The UN Security Council opposed the invasion and the territory's nominal status in the UN remained as "non-self-governing territory under Portuguese administration".<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span id="Indonesian_occupation_.281975.E2.80.931999.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Indonesian_occupation_(1975–1999)">Indonesian occupation (1975–1999)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Timor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Indonesian occupation (1975–1999)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:East_Timor_Demo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/East_Timor_Demo.jpg/220px-East_Timor_Demo.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/East_Timor_Demo.jpg/330px-East_Timor_Demo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/East_Timor_Demo.jpg/440px-East_Timor_Demo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:East_Timor_Demo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A demonstration for <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_occupation_of_East_Timor" title="Indonesian occupation of East Timor">independence from Indonesia</a> held in Australia during September 1999
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Indonesian_occupation_of_East_Timor" title="Indonesian occupation of East Timor">Indonesia's occupation of East Timor</a> was marked by violence and brutality. A detailed statistical report prepared for the <a href="/wiki/Commission_for_Reception,_Truth_and_Reconciliation_in_East_Timor" title="Commission for Reception, Truth and Reconciliation in East Timor">Commission for Reception, Truth and Reconciliation in East Timor</a> cited a minimum of 102,800 conflict-related deaths in the period 1974–1999, namely, approximately 18,600 killings and 84,200 "excess" deaths from hunger and illness, with an estimated figure based on Portuguese, Indonesian and Catholic Church data of approximately 200,000 deaths.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> The East Timorese guerrilla force (Forças Armadas da Libertação Nacional de Timor-Leste, <a href="/wiki/Falintil" title="Falintil">Falintil</a>) fought a campaign against the Indonesian forces from 1975 to 1998.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The 1991 <a href="/wiki/Dili_Massacre" class="mw-redirect" title="Dili Massacre">Dili Massacre</a> was a turning point for the independence cause and an East Timor solidarity movement grew in Portugal, the Philippines, Australia, and other Western countries. </p>
      <p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Suharto" title="Fall of Suharto">resignation of Indonesian President Suharto</a>, an UN-sponsored agreement between Indonesia and Portugal allowed for an UN-supervised popular <a href="/wiki/East_Timorese_independence_referendum,_1999" class="mw-redirect" title="East Timorese independence referendum, 1999">referendum</a> in August 1999. A clear vote for independence was met with a <a href="/wiki/1999_East_Timorese_crisis" title="1999 East Timorese crisis">punitive campaign of violence</a> by East Timorese <a href="/wiki/Pro-Indonesia_militia" title="Pro-Indonesia militia">pro-integration militia</a> supported by elements of the Indonesian military. This allowed the sending of the multinational peacekeeping force, <a href="/wiki/International_Force_East_Timor" title="International Force East Timor">INTERFET</a>, which was formed by Australia, the Philippines, South Korea, Thailand, and New Zealand, with aid from the United States, to restore order and aid East Timorese refugees and internally-displaced persons.<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-42">[42]</a></sup> On 25 October 1999, the administration of East Timor was taken over by the UN through the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Transitional_Administration_in_East_Timor" title="United Nations Transitional Administration in East Timor">United Nations Transitional Administration in East Timor</a> (UNTAET), headed by <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Vieira_de_Mello" class="mw-redirect" title="Sergio Vieira de Mello">Sergio Vieira de Mello</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> The INTERFET deployment ended in February 2000 with the transfer of military command to the UN.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary_era">Contemporary era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Timor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Contemporary era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Pr%C3%A4sidentschaftswalhkampf_JRH_2007.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Pr%C3%A4sidentschaftswalhkampf_JRH_2007.JPG/170px-Pr%C3%A4sidentschaftswalhkampf_JRH_2007.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Pr%C3%A4sidentschaftswalhkampf_JRH_2007.JPG/255px-Pr%C3%A4sidentschaftswalhkampf_JRH_2007.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Pr%C3%A4sidentschaftswalhkampf_JRH_2007.JPG/340px-Pr%C3%A4sidentschaftswalhkampf_JRH_2007.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="3264"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Pr%C3%A4sidentschaftswalhkampf_JRH_2007.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Ramos-Horta" title="José Ramos-Horta">José Ramos-Horta</a>, 1996 Nobel Peace Prize winner, second President of East Timor
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On 30 August 2001, the East Timorese voted in their first election organised by the UN to elect members of the Constituent Assembly.<sup id="cite_ref-ConstitENG_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ConstitENG-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UNOct01_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNOct01-46">[46]</a></sup> On 22 March 2002, the Constituent Assembly approved the Constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-ConstitENG_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ConstitENG-20">[20]</a></sup> By May 2002, over 205,000 refugees had returned.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> On 20 May 2002, the Constitution of the Democratic Republic of East Timor came into force and East Timor was recognised as independent by the UN.<sup id="cite_ref-UNOct01_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNOct01-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> The Constituent Assembly was renamed the National Parliament and <a href="/wiki/Xanana_Gusm%C3%A3o" title="Xanana Gusmão">Xanana Gusmão</a> was sworn in as the country's first President after Indonesian occupation. On 27 September 2002, East Timor was renamed Timor-Leste, using the Portuguese language, and was admitted as a member state by the UN.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2006, the United Nations sent in security forces to restore order when unrest and factional fighting forced 15 percent of the population (155,000 people) to flee their homes.<sup id="cite_ref-abc_2012-12-30_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abc_2012-12-30-50">[50]</a></sup> The following year, Gusmão declined another presidential term, and in the build-up to the <a href="/wiki/East_Timorese_presidential_election,_2007" class="mw-redirect" title="East Timorese presidential election, 2007">mid-year presidential elections</a> there were renewed outbreaks of violence. In those elections, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Ramos-Horta" title="José Ramos-Horta">José Ramos-Horta</a> was elected <a href="/wiki/President_of_East_Timor" title="President of East Timor">President</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> In June 2007, Gusmão ran in the <a href="/wiki/East_Timorese_parliamentary_election,_2007" class="mw-redirect" title="East Timorese parliamentary election, 2007">parliamentary elections</a> and became Prime Minister. In February 2008, Ramos-Horta was critically injured in <a href="/wiki/2008_East_Timor_coup_attempt" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 East Timor coup attempt">an attempted assassination</a>. Prime Minister Gusmão also faced gunfire separately but escaped unharmed. Australian reinforcements were immediately sent to help keep order.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> In March 2011, the UN handed over operational control of the police force to the East Timor authorities. The United Nations ended its peacekeeping mission on 31 December 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-abc_2012-12-30_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abc_2012-12-30-50">[50]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>East Timor became a state party to the <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Convention" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage Convention">World Heritage Convention</a> on 31 January 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_government">Politics and government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Timor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Politics and government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Xanana_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Xanana_2011.jpg/170px-Xanana_2011.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="212" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Xanana_2011.jpg/255px-Xanana_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Xanana_2011.jpg/340px-Xanana_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1381" data-file-height="1720"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Xanana_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Xanana_Gusm%C3%A3o" title="Xanana Gusmão">Xanana Gusmão</a>, the first East Timorese President after Indonesian occupation.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_East_Timor" title="Politics of East Timor">Politics of East Timor</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> of East Timor is the <a href="/wiki/President_of_East_Timor" title="President of East Timor">President of the Republic</a>, who is elected by popular vote for a five-year term. Although the President's executive powers are somewhat limited, he or she does have the power to appoint the Prime Minister and veto government legislation. Following elections, the President usually appoints the leader of the majority party or <a href="/wiki/Coalition" title="Coalition">coalition</a> as <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_East_Timor" title="Prime Minister of East Timor">Prime Minister of East Timor</a> and the cabinet on the proposal of the latter. As <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>, the Prime Minister presides over the cabinet.<sup id="cite_ref-Divided_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Divided-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SpL_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SpL-5">[5]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Pr%C3%A4sidentenpalast_17-05-2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Pr%C3%A4sidentenpalast_17-05-2015.jpg/220px-Pr%C3%A4sidentenpalast_17-05-2015.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Pr%C3%A4sidentenpalast_17-05-2015.jpg/330px-Pr%C3%A4sidentenpalast_17-05-2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Pr%C3%A4sidentenpalast_17-05-2015.jpg/440px-Pr%C3%A4sidentenpalast_17-05-2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="476"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Pr%C3%A4sidentenpalast_17-05-2015.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Nicolau_Lobato_Presidential_Palace" title="Nicolau Lobato Presidential Palace">Nicolau Lobato Presidential Palace</a> in Dili.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Unicameral" class="mw-redirect" title="Unicameral">unicameral</a> East Timorese parliament is the <a href="/wiki/National_Parliament_(East_Timor)" title="National Parliament (East Timor)">National Parliament</a> or <i>Parlamento Nacional</i>, the members of which are elected by popular vote to a five-year term. The number of seats can vary from a minimum of fifty-two to a maximum of sixty-five. The East Timorese constitution was modelled on that of Portugal. The country is still in the process of building its administration and governmental institutions. Government departments include the <a href="/wiki/Pol%C3%ADcia_Nacional_de_Timor-Leste" class="mw-redirect" title="Polícia Nacional de Timor-Leste">Polícia Nacional de Timor-Leste</a> (police), East Timor Ministry for State and Internal Administration, <a href="/wiki/Civil_Aviation_Division_of_Timor-Leste" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil Aviation Division of Timor-Leste">Civil Aviation Division of Timor-Leste</a>, and Immigration Department of Timor-Leste.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_enforcement">Law enforcement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Timor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Law enforcement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Police_of_East_Timor" title="National Police of East Timor">National Police of East Timor</a> or PNTL is the national police force of East Timor, established in May 2002 by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, before sovereignty was passed to the new state, with a mandate to provide security and maintain law and order throughout the country, and to enable the rapid development of a credible, professional and impartial police service. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Timor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_East_Timor" title="Municipalities of East Timor">Municipalities of East Timor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Administrative_posts_of_East_Timor" title="Administrative posts of East Timor">Administrative posts of East Timor</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sucos_of_East_Timor" title="Sucos of East Timor">Sucos of East Timor</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:442px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Municipalities_of_Timor-Leste.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Municipalities_of_Timor-Leste.png/440px-Municipalities_of_Timor-Leste.png" decoding="async" width="440" height="254" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Municipalities_of_Timor-Leste.png/660px-Municipalities_of_Timor-Leste.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Municipalities_of_Timor-Leste.png/880px-Municipalities_of_Timor-Leste.png 2x" data-file-width="3344" data-file-height="1929"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Municipalities_of_Timor-Leste.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The thirteen municipalities of East Timor
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>East Timor is divided into thirteen municipalities, which in turn are subdivided into 65 administrative posts, 442 <i>sucos</i> (villages), and 2,225 <i>aldeias</i> (hamlets).<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ol>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Oecusse" title="Oecusse">Oecusse</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Liqui%C3%A7%C3%A1_Municipality" title="Liquiçá Municipality">Liquiçá</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Dili_Municipality" title="Dili Municipality">Dili</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Manatuto_Municipality" title="Manatuto Municipality">Manatuto</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Baucau_Municipality" title="Baucau Municipality">Baucau</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Laut%C3%A9m_Municipality" title="Lautém Municipality">Lautém</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Bobonaro_Municipality" title="Bobonaro Municipality">Bobonaro</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Ermera_Municipality" title="Ermera Municipality">Ermera</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Aileu_Municipality" title="Aileu Municipality">Aileu</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Viqueque_Municipality" title="Viqueque Municipality">Viqueque</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Cova_Lima_Municipality" title="Cova Lima Municipality">Cova Lima</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Ainaro_Municipality" title="Ainaro Municipality">Ainaro</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Manufahi_Municipality" title="Manufahi Municipality">Manufahi</a></li>
      </ol> 
      <p>Articles 5 and 71 of the 2002 constitution provide that Oecusse be governed by a special administrative policy and economic regime. Law 3/2014 of 18 June 2014 created the Special Administrative Region of Oe-Cusse Ambeno (Região Administrativa Especial de Oecusse, RAEOA).<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations_and_military">Foreign relations and military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Timor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Foreign relations and military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_East_Timor" title="Foreign relations of East Timor">Foreign relations of East Timor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timor_Leste_Defence_Force" title="Timor Leste Defence Force">Timor Leste Defence Force</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Timor-Leste_Defense_Forces_soldiers_in_military_training.png" class="image"><img alt="Timor-Leste Defense Forces soldiers in military training" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Timor-Leste_Defense_Forces_soldiers_in_military_training.png/220px-Timor-Leste_Defense_Forces_soldiers_in_military_training.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Timor-Leste_Defense_Forces_soldiers_in_military_training.png/330px-Timor-Leste_Defense_Forces_soldiers_in_military_training.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Timor-Leste_Defense_Forces_soldiers_in_military_training.png/440px-Timor-Leste_Defense_Forces_soldiers_in_military_training.png 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="853"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Timor-Leste_Defense_Forces_soldiers_in_military_training.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Timor-Leste Defense Forces soldiers in military training
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>East Timor is a full member state of the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Community of Portuguese Language Countries</a> (CPLP), also known as the Lusophone Commonwealth, an international organisation and political association of <a href="/wiki/Lusophone" title="Lusophone">Lusophone</a> nations across four continents. In each of those nations, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> is an official language. East Timor sought membership in the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Southeast_Asian_Nations" class="mw-redirect" title="Association of Southeast Asian Nations">Association of Southeast Asian Nations</a> (ASEAN) in 2007, and a formal application was submitted in March 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The East Timor Defence Force (<i>Forças de Defesa de Timor-Leste</i>, F-FDTL) is the <a href="/wiki/Armed_forces" class="mw-redirect" title="Armed forces">military body</a> responsible for the defence of East Timor. The F-FDTL was established in February 2001 and comprised two small infantry battalions, a small naval component, and several supporting units. </p>
      <p>F-FDTL's primary role is to protect East Timor from external threats. It also has an internal security role, which overlaps with that of the <a href="/wiki/National_Police_of_East_Timor" title="National Police of East Timor">National Police of East Timor</a> (Polícia Nacional de Timor-Leste, PNTL). This overlap has led to tensions between the services, which have been exacerbated by poor morale and lack of discipline within the F-FDTL.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The F-FDTL's problems <a href="/wiki/2006_East_Timorese_crisis" title="2006 East Timorese crisis">came to a head in 2006</a> when almost half the force was dismissed following protests over discrimination and poor conditions. The dismissal contributed to a general collapse of both the F-FDTL and PNTL in May and forced the government to request foreign peacekeepers to restore security. The F-FDTL is being rebuilt with foreign assistance and has drawn up a long-term force development plan. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Oil_demo_Timor_2013.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Oil_demo_Timor_2013.JPG/220px-Oil_demo_Timor_2013.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Oil_demo_Timor_2013.JPG/330px-Oil_demo_Timor_2013.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Oil_demo_Timor_2013.JPG/440px-Oil_demo_Timor_2013.JPG 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="474"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Oil_demo_Timor_2013.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Demonstration against Australia in December 2013
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Since the discovery of petroleum in the Timor Sea in the 1970s, there have been disputes surrounding the rights to ownership and exploitation of the resources situated in a part of the Timor Sea known as the <a href="/wiki/Timor_Gap" title="Timor Gap">Timor Gap</a>, which is the area of the Timor Sea which lies outside the territorial boundaries of the nations to the north and south of the Timor Sea.<sup id="cite_ref-ta_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ta-58">[58]</a></sup> These disagreements initially involved Australia and Indonesia, although a resolution was eventually reached in the form of the <a href="/wiki/Timor_Gap_Treaty" title="Timor Gap Treaty">Timor Gap Treaty</a>. After the declaration of East Timor's nationhood in 1999, the terms of the Timor Gap Treaty were abandoned and negotiations commenced between Australia and East Timor, culminating in the <a href="/wiki/Timor_Sea_Treaty" title="Timor Sea Treaty">Timor Sea Treaty</a>. </p>
      <p>Australia's territorial claim extended to the bathymetric axis (the line of greatest sea-bed depth) at the Timor Trough. It overlapped East Timor's own territorial claim, which followed the former colonial power <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Convention_on_the_Law_of_the_Sea" title="United Nations Convention on the Law of the Sea">United Nations Convention on the Law of the Sea</a> in claiming that the dividing line should be midway between the two countries. </p>
      <p>It was revealed in 2013 that the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Secret_Intelligence_Service" title="Australian Secret Intelligence Service">Australian Secret Intelligence Service</a> (ASIS) planted listening devices to listen to the East Timorese government during negotiations over the Greater Sunrise oil and gas fields. This is known as the <a href="/wiki/Australia%E2%80%93East_Timor_spying_scandal" title="Australia–East Timor spying scandal">Australia–East Timor spying scandal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Timor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_East_Timor" title="Geography of East Timor">Geography of East Timor</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Located in between Southeast Asia and Oceania,<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> the island of <a href="/wiki/Timor" title="Timor">Timor</a> is part of <a href="/wiki/Maritime_Southeast_Asia" title="Maritime Southeast Asia">Maritime Southeast Asia</a>, and is the largest and easternmost of the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Sunda_Islands" title="Lesser Sunda Islands">Lesser Sunda Islands</a>. To the north of the island are the <a href="/wiki/Ombai_Strait" title="Ombai Strait">Ombai Strait</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wetar_Strait" title="Wetar Strait">Wetar Strait</a>, and the greater <a href="/wiki/Banda_Sea" title="Banda Sea">Banda Sea</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Timor_Sea" title="Timor Sea">Timor Sea</a> separates the island from <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> to the south, and the <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Indonesia" title="Provinces of Indonesia">Indonesian province</a> of <a href="/wiki/East_Nusa_Tenggara" title="East Nusa Tenggara">East Nusa Tenggara</a> lies to East Timor's west. The total land size is 14,919&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (5,760&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). East Timor has an <a href="/wiki/Exclusive_economic_zone" title="Exclusive economic zone">exclusive economic zone</a> of 70,326&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (27,153&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Much of the country is mountainous, and its highest point is <a href="/wiki/Tatamailau" title="Tatamailau">Tatamailau</a> (also known as Mount Ramelau) at 2,963 metres (9,721&nbsp;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-gb_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gb-62">[62]</a></sup> The climate is tropical and generally hot and humid. It is characterised by distinct rainy and dry seasons. The capital, largest city, and main port is Dili, and the second-largest city is the eastern town of <a href="/wiki/Baucau" title="Baucau">Baucau</a>. East Timor lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/8th_parallel_south" title="8th parallel south">8°</a> and <a href="/wiki/10th_parallel_south" title="10th parallel south">10°S</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/124th_meridian_east" title="124th meridian east">124°</a> and <a href="/wiki/128th_meridian_east" title="128th meridian east">128°E</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_TLS_present.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Koppen-Geiger_Map_TLS_present.svg/220px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_TLS_present.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="104" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Koppen-Geiger_Map_TLS_present.svg/330px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_TLS_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Koppen-Geiger_Map_TLS_present.svg/440px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_TLS_present.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1794" data-file-height="850"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_TLS_present.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> map for East Timor.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The easternmost area of East Timor consists of the <a href="/wiki/Paitchau" title="Paitchau">Paitchau</a> Range and the Lake <a href="/wiki/Ira_Lalaro" title="Ira Lalaro">Ira Lalaro</a> area, which contains the country's first conservation area, the <a href="/wiki/Nino_Konis_Santana_National_Park" title="Nino Konis Santana National Park">Nino Konis Santana National Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> It contains the last remaining <a href="/wiki/Tropical_dry" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical dry">tropical dry</a> forested area within the country. It hosts a number of unique plant and animal species and is sparsely populated.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> The northern coast is characterised by a number of <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">coral reef</a> systems that have been determined to be at risk.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>East Timor is home to the <a href="/wiki/Timor_and_Wetar_deciduous_forests" title="Timor and Wetar deciduous forests">Timor and Wetar deciduous forests</a> ecoregion.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-66">[66]</a></sup> It had a 2018 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 7.11/10, ranking it 57th globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-67">[67]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Timor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_East_Timor" title="Economy of East Timor">Economy of East Timor</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Economy_of_East_Timor_(nominal_GDP)(previous_and_data).png" class="image"><img alt="Economy of East Timor (nominal GDP)(previous and data)" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Economy_of_East_Timor_%28nominal_GDP%29%28previous_and_data%29.png/220px-Economy_of_East_Timor_%28nominal_GDP%29%28previous_and_data%29.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Economy_of_East_Timor_%28nominal_GDP%29%28previous_and_data%29.png/330px-Economy_of_East_Timor_%28nominal_GDP%29%28previous_and_data%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Economy_of_East_Timor_%28nominal_GDP%29%28previous_and_data%29.png/440px-Economy_of_East_Timor_%28nominal_GDP%29%28previous_and_data%29.png 2x" data-file-width="957" data-file-height="611"></a>

        </div>
       </div>
      </div>

       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:DSCI2950_Timor_Plaza.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/DSCI2950_Timor_Plaza.jpg/220px-DSCI2950_Timor_Plaza.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/DSCI2950_Timor_Plaza.jpg/330px-DSCI2950_Timor_Plaza.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/DSCI2950_Timor_Plaza.jpg/440px-DSCI2950_Timor_Plaza.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5152" data-file-height="3864"></a>

        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:ANL_Timor_Trader,_Dili,_2018_(02).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/ANL_Timor_Trader%2C_Dili%2C_2018_%2802%29.jpg/220px-ANL_Timor_Trader%2C_Dili%2C_2018_%2802%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/ANL_Timor_Trader%2C_Dili%2C_2018_%2802%29.jpg/330px-ANL_Timor_Trader%2C_Dili%2C_2018_%2802%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/ANL_Timor_Trader%2C_Dili%2C_2018_%2802%29.jpg/440px-ANL_Timor_Trader%2C_Dili%2C_2018_%2802%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4481" data-file-height="3460"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:ANL_Timor_Trader,_Dili,_2018_(02).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Port of Dili
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The economy of East Timor is a <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economy</a>, which used to depend upon exports of a few commodities such as <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marble" title="Marble">marble</a>, <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">petroleum</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sandalwood" title="Sandalwood">sandalwood</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-debrowser_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-debrowser-68">[68]</a></sup> It grew by about 10% in 2011 and at a similar rate in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>East Timor now has revenue from offshore oil and gas reserves, but little of it has been spent on the development of villages, which still rely on subsistence farming.<sup id="cite_ref-Schonhardt_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schonhardt-70">[70]</a></sup> As of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=East_Timor&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, nearly half the East Timorese population was living in extreme poverty.<sup id="cite_ref-Schonhardt_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schonhardt-70">[70]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Timor-Leste_Petroleum_Fund" title="Timor-Leste Petroleum Fund">Timor-Leste Petroleum Fund</a> was established in 2005, and by 2011 it had reached a worth of US$8.7 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-irin-asia_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-irin-asia-71">[71]</a></sup> East Timor is labelled by the International Monetary Fund as the "most oil-dependent economy in the world".<sup id="cite_ref-art4_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-art4-72">[72]</a></sup> The Petroleum Fund pays for nearly all of the government's annual budget, which increased from $70 million in 2004 to $1.3 billion in 2011, with a $1.8 billion proposal for 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-irin-asia_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-irin-asia-71">[71]</a></sup> East-Timor's income from oil and gas stands to increase significantly after its cancellation of a controversial agreement with Australia, which gave Australia half of the income from oil and gas from 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The country's economy is dependent on government spending and, to a lesser extent, assistance from foreign donors.<sup id="cite_ref-us-dos_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-us-dos-74">[74]</a></sup> Private sector development has lagged due to human capital shortages, infrastructure weakness, an incomplete legal system, and an inefficient regulatory environment.<sup id="cite_ref-us-dos_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-us-dos-74">[74]</a></sup> After <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">petroleum</a>, the second largest export is <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a>, which generates about $10 million a year.<sup id="cite_ref-us-dos_74-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-us-dos-74">[74]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Starbucks" title="Starbucks">Starbucks</a> is a major purchaser of East Timorese coffee.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:167px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Timor_Lorosa%27e_centavo_coin_-2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Timor_Lorosa%27e_centavo_coin_-2.JPG/165px-Timor_Lorosa%27e_centavo_coin_-2.JPG" decoding="async" width="165" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Timor_Lorosa%27e_centavo_coin_-2.JPG/247px-Timor_Lorosa%27e_centavo_coin_-2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Timor_Lorosa%27e_centavo_coin_-2.JPG/329px-Timor_Lorosa%27e_centavo_coin_-2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2009" data-file-height="2073"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Timor_Lorosa%27e_centavo_coin_-2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Fractional coins "centavos"
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p> 9,000 tonnes of coffee, 108 tonnes of <a href="/wiki/Cinnamon" title="Cinnamon">cinnamon</a> and 161 tonnes of cocoa were harvested in 2012 making the country the 40th ranked producer of coffee, the 6th ranked producer of cinnamon and the 50th ranked producer of cocoa worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to data gathered in the 2010 census, 87.7% of urban (321,043 people) and 18.9% of rural (821,459 people) households have electricity, for an overall average of 38.2%.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The agriculture sector employs 80% of East Timor's active population.<sup id="cite_ref-wb-expanding_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wb-expanding-78">[78]</a></sup> In 2009, about 67,000 households grew coffee in East Timor, with a large proportion of those households being poor.<sup id="cite_ref-wb-expanding_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wb-expanding-78">[78]</a></sup> Currently, the <a href="/wiki/Gross_margin" title="Gross margin">gross margins</a> are about $120 per hectare, with returns per labour-day of about $3.70.<sup id="cite_ref-wb-expanding_78-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wb-expanding-78">[78]</a></sup> There were 11,000 households growing <a href="/wiki/Mung_bean" title="Mung bean">mungbeans</a> as of 2009, most of them by subsistence farming.<sup id="cite_ref-wb-expanding_78-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wb-expanding-78">[78]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Ease_of_doing_business_index" title="Ease of doing business index">Doing Business</a> 2013 report by the World Bank, East Timor was ranked 169th overall and last in the East Asia and Pacific region. The country fared particularly poorly in the "registering property", "enforcing contracts" and "resolving insolvency" categories, ranking last worldwide in all three.<sup id="cite_ref-edb_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-edb-79">[79]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As regards telecommunications infrastructure, East Timor is the second to last ranked Asian country in the World Economic Forum's Network Readiness Index (NRI), with only <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a> falling behind it in southeast Asia. NRI is an indicator for determining the development level of a country's information and communication technologies. In the 2014 NRI ranking, East Timor ranked number 141 overall, down from 134 in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Portuguese colonial administration granted concessions to the Australia-bound Oceanic Exploration Corporation to develop petroleum and natural gas deposits in the waters southeast of Timor. However, this was curtailed by the Indonesian invasion in 1976.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The resources were divided between Indonesia and Australia with the <a href="/wiki/Timor_Gap_Treaty" title="Timor Gap Treaty">Timor Gap Treaty</a> in 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> East Timor inherited no permanent maritime boundaries when it attained independence.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> A provisional agreement (the <a href="/wiki/Timor_Sea_Treaty" title="Timor Sea Treaty">Timor Sea Treaty</a>, signed when East Timor became independent on 20 May 2002) defined a Joint Petroleum Development Area (JPDA) and awarded 90% of revenues from existing projects in that area to East Timor and 10% to Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> An agreement in 2005 between the governments of East Timor and Australia mandated that both countries put aside their dispute over maritime boundaries and that East Timor would receive 50% of the revenues from the resource exploitation in the area (estimated at <a href="/wiki/Australian_Dollar" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian Dollar">A$</a>26 billion, or about US$20 billion over the lifetime of the project)<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> from the Greater Sunrise development.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> In 2013, East Timor launched a case at the <a href="/wiki/Permanent_Court_of_Arbitration" title="Permanent Court of Arbitration">Permanent Court of Arbitration</a> in <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a> to pull out of a gas treaty that it had signed with Australia, accusing the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Secret_Intelligence_Service" title="Australian Secret Intelligence Service">Australian Secret Intelligence Service</a> (ASIS) of <a href="/wiki/Covert_listening_device" title="Covert listening device">bugging</a> the East Timorese cabinet room in Dili in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-ABC_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC-85">[85]</a></sup> East Timor is part of the <a href="/wiki/Timor_Leste%E2%80%93Indonesia%E2%80%93Australia_Growth_Triangle" title="Timor Leste–Indonesia–Australia Growth Triangle">Timor Leste–Indonesia–Australia Growth Triangle</a> (TIA-GT).<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are no <a href="/wiki/Patent" title="Patent">patent laws</a> in East Timor.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A railway system has been proposed but the current government has yet to approve the proposal due to lack of funds and expertise.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Timor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Tourism is still of minor importance in East Timor. In 2017, the country was visited by 75,000 tourists.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> Since the later 2010s, tourism has been increasing and the number of hotels and resorts has increased. The government decided to invest in the expansion of the international airport in Dili. </p>
      <p>The risk for tourists in East Timor is medium/low, with positive factors being a low crime, the occurrence of zero terrorist attacks in the last decades and road safety. Negative factors for tourists include roads in poor condition, mainly in the interior of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Timor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
