      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:East_Timor_demographic_change.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/East_Timor_demographic_change.png/220px-East_Timor_demographic_change.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/East_Timor_demographic_change.png/330px-East_Timor_demographic_change.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/East_Timor_demographic_change.png/440px-East_Timor_demographic_change.png 2x" data-file-width="675" data-file-height="397"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:East_Timor_demographic_change.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>East Timor demographic change between 1861 and 2010.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>East Timor recorded a population of 1,183,643 in its 2015 census.<sup id="cite_ref-census_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census-8">[8]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The CIA's World Factbook lists the English-language demonym for East Timor as Timorese,<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> as does the Government of Timor-Leste's website.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> Other reference sources list it as East Timorese.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The word <i>Maubere</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> formerly used by the Portuguese to refer to native East Timorese and often employed as synonymous with the illiterate and uneducated, was adopted by Fretilin as a term of pride.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> Native East Timorese consist of a number of distinct ethnic groups, the largest Malayo-Polynesian ethnic groups are the <a href="/wiki/Tetum" class="mw-redirect" title="Tetum">Tetum</a><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> (100,000), primarily in the north coast and around Dili; the <a href="/wiki/Mambai_people_(Timor)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mambai people (Timor)">Mambai</a> (80,000), in the central mountains; the <a href="/wiki/Tukudede" class="mw-redirect" title="Tukudede">Tukudede</a> (63,170), in the area around <a href="/wiki/Maubara" title="Maubara">Maubara</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liqui%C3%A7%C3%A1" title="Liquiçá">Liquiçá</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Galoli" class="mw-redirect" title="Galoli">Galoli</a> (50,000), between the tribes of Mambae and <a href="/wiki/Makasae" class="mw-redirect" title="Makasae">Makasae</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Kemak_people" title="Kemak people">Kemak</a> (50,000) in north-central Timor island; and the <a href="/wiki/Baikeno" class="mw-redirect" title="Baikeno">Baikeno</a> (20,000), in the area around <a href="/wiki/Pante_Macassar" title="Pante Macassar">Pante Macassar</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The main tribes of predominantly Papuan origin include the <a href="/wiki/Bunak" class="mw-redirect" title="Bunak">Bunak</a> (84,000), in the central interior of Timor island; the <a href="/wiki/Fataluku_language" title="Fataluku language">Fataluku</a> (40,000), at the eastern tip of the island near <a href="/wiki/Lospalos" title="Lospalos">Lospalos</a>; and the <a href="/wiki/Makasae" class="mw-redirect" title="Makasae">Makasae</a> (70,000), toward the eastern end of the island.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> As a result of <a href="/wiki/Interracial_marriage" title="Interracial marriage">interracial marriage</a> which was common during the Portuguese era, there is a population of people of mixed East Timorese and Portuguese origin, known in Portuguese as <i><a href="/wiki/Mesti%C3%A7o" title="Mestiço">mestiços</a></i>. There is a small <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">Chinese</a> minority, most of whom are <a href="/wiki/Hakka_people#East_Timor" title="Hakka people">Hakka</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> Many Chinese left in the mid-1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Timor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_East_Timor" title="Languages of East Timor">Languages of East Timor</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sprachen_Osttimors-en.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Sprachen_Osttimors-en.png/300px-Sprachen_Osttimors-en.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="199" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Sprachen_Osttimors-en.png/450px-Sprachen_Osttimors-en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Sprachen_Osttimors-en.png/600px-Sprachen_Osttimors-en.png 2x" data-file-width="1354" data-file-height="900"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sprachen_Osttimors-en.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Major language groups in East Timor by <i><a href="/wiki/Suco" class="mw-redirect" title="Suco">suco</a></i>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>East Timor's two official languages are <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tetum_language" title="Tetum language">Tetum</a>. In addition, <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a> are designated by the constitution as "working languages".<sup id="cite_ref-thejakartapost.com_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thejakartapost.com-101">[101]</a></sup> Tetum belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_languages" title="Austronesian languages">Austronesian</a> family of languages spoken throughout Southeast Asia and the Pacific.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The 2015 census found that the most commonly spoken <a href="/wiki/Mother_tongue" class="mw-redirect" title="Mother tongue">mother tongues</a> were <a href="/wiki/Tetum_language" title="Tetum language">Tetum Prasa</a> (mother tongue for 30.6% of the population), <a href="/wiki/Mambai_language_(Timor)" title="Mambai language (Timor)">Mambai</a> (16.6%), <a href="/wiki/Makasai" class="mw-redirect" title="Makasai">Makasai</a> (10.5%), <a href="/wiki/Tetum_language" title="Tetum language">Tetum Terik</a> (6.05%), <a href="/wiki/Baikenu" class="mw-redirect" title="Baikenu">Baikenu</a> (5.87%), <a href="/wiki/Kemak_language" title="Kemak language">Kemak</a> (5.85%), <a href="/wiki/Bunak_language" title="Bunak language">Bunak</a> (5.48%), <a href="/wiki/Tokodede" class="mw-redirect" title="Tokodede">Tokodede</a> (3.97%), and <a href="/wiki/Fataluku_language" title="Fataluku language">Fataluku</a> (3.52%). Other indigenous languages accounted for 10.47%, while 1.09% of the population spoke foreign languages natively.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Under <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_occupation_of_East_Timor" title="Indonesian occupation of East Timor">Indonesian rule</a>, the use of <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> was banned and only <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a> was allowed to be used in government offices, schools and public business.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> During the Indonesian occupation, Tetum and Portuguese were important unifying elements for the East Timorese people in opposing <a href="/wiki/Javanese_culture" title="Javanese culture">Javanese culture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> Portuguese was adopted as one of the two official languages upon independence in 2002 for this reason and as a link to <a href="/wiki/Lusophone" title="Lusophone">Lusophone</a> nations in other parts of the world. It is now being taught and promoted with the help of Brazil, Portugal, and the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Community of Portuguese Language Countries</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to the observatory of the Portuguese language, the East Timorese literacy rate was 77.8% in Tetum, 55.6% in Indonesian, and 39.3% in Portuguese, and that the primary literacy rate increased from 73% in 2009 to 83% in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-ILLP_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ILLP-107">[107]</a></sup> Indonesian and English are defined as working languages under the Constitution in the Final and Transitional Provisions, without setting a final date. In 2012, 35% could speak, read, and write Portuguese, which is up significantly from less than 5% in the 2006 UN Development Report. Portuguese is recovering as it is now been made the main official language of Timor, and is being taught in most schools.<sup id="cite_ref-thejakartapost.com_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thejakartapost.com-101">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> According to the 2015 census, 50% of the population between the ages of 14 and 24 can speak and understand Portuguese.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> It is estimated that English is understood by 31.4% of the population. East Timor is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Community of Portuguese Language Countries</a> (also known as the <a href="/wiki/Lusophone" title="Lusophone">Lusophone</a> Commonwealth) and of the <a href="/wiki/Latin_Union" title="Latin Union">Latin Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Aside from Tetum, <a href="/wiki/Ethnologue" title="Ethnologue">Ethnologue</a> lists the following indigenous languages: <a href="/wiki/Adabe_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Adabe language">Adabe</a>, Baikeno, Bunak, Fataluku, <a href="/wiki/Galoli_language" title="Galoli language">Galoli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Habun_language" title="Habun language">Habun</a>, <a href="/wiki/Idat%C3%A9" class="mw-redirect" title="Idaté">Idaté</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kairui-Midiki_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Kairui-Midiki language">Kairui-Midiki</a>, Kemak, <a href="/wiki/Lakalei_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Lakalei language">Lakalei</a>, Makasae, <a href="/wiki/Makuv%27a" class="mw-redirect" title="Makuv'a">Makuv'a</a>, Mambae, <a href="/wiki/Nauete_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Nauete language">Nauete</a>, Tukudede, and <a href="/wiki/Waima%27a_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Waima'a language">Waima'a</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Atlas_of_the_World%27s_Languages_in_Danger" class="mw-redirect" title="Atlas of the World's Languages in Danger">Atlas of the World's Languages in Danger</a>, there are six endangered languages in East Timor: <a href="/wiki/Adabe" class="mw-redirect" title="Adabe">Adabe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Habu_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Habu language">Habu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kairui-Midiki" class="mw-redirect" title="Kairui-Midiki">Kairui-Midiki</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maku%27a_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Maku'a language">Maku'a</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naueti_language" title="Naueti language">Naueti</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Waima%27a_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Waima'a language">Waima'a</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Timor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Portuguese_School_of_D%C3%ADli,_Timor-Leste.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Portuguese_School_of_D%C3%ADli%2C_Timor-Leste.jpg/220px-Portuguese_School_of_D%C3%ADli%2C_Timor-Leste.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="123" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Portuguese_School_of_D%C3%ADli%2C_Timor-Leste.jpg/330px-Portuguese_School_of_D%C3%ADli%2C_Timor-Leste.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Portuguese_School_of_D%C3%ADli%2C_Timor-Leste.jpg/440px-Portuguese_School_of_D%C3%ADli%2C_Timor-Leste.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3344" data-file-height="1872"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Portuguese_School_of_D%C3%ADli,_Timor-Leste.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Escola_Portuguesa_Ruy_Cinatti" title="Escola Portuguesa Ruy Cinatti">Escola Portuguesa Ruy Cinatti</a>, the Portuguese School of Díli.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>East Timor's adult <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">literacy</a> rate in 2010 was 58.3%, up from 37.6% in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-unescolit_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unescolit-113">[113]</a></sup> At the end of Portuguese rule, literacy was at 5%.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The country's main university is the <a href="/wiki/National_University_of_East_Timor" title="National University of East Timor">National University of East Timor</a>. There are also four colleges.<sup id="cite_ref-robinson_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-robinson-115">[115]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since independence, both <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a> and Tetum have lost ground as <a href="/wiki/Medium_of_instruction" title="Medium of instruction">media of instruction</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> has increased: in 2001 only 8.4% of primary school and 6.8% of secondary school students attended a Portuguese-medium school; by 2005 this had increased to 81.6% for primary and 46.3% for secondary schools.<sup id="cite_ref-edulang_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-edulang-116">[116]</a></sup> Indonesian formerly played a considerable role in education, being used by 73.7% of all secondary school students as a medium of instruction, but by 2005 Portuguese was used by most schools in <a href="/wiki/Baucau_District" class="mw-redirect" title="Baucau District">Baucau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manatuto_District" class="mw-redirect" title="Manatuto District">Manatuto</a>, as well as the capital district.<sup id="cite_ref-edulang_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-edulang-116">[116]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> has sent Filipino teachers to East Timor to teach <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, so as to facilitate a program between the two countries, under which deserving East Timorese nationals with English language skills will be granted university scholarships in the Philippines.<sup id="cite_ref-edulang_116-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-edulang-116">[116]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Timor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>See <a href="/wiki/Health_in_East_Timor" title="Health in East Timor">Health in East Timor</a> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Timor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_East_Timor" title="Religion in East Timor">Religion in East Timor</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_in_East_Timor" title="Catholic Church in East Timor">Catholic Church in East Timor</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Motael_Church,_Dili,_East_Timor_(312012049).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Motael_Church%2C_Dili%2C_East_Timor_%28312012049%29.jpg/170px-Motael_Church%2C_Dili%2C_East_Timor_%28312012049%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="230" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Motael_Church%2C_Dili%2C_East_Timor_%28312012049%29.jpg/255px-Motael_Church%2C_Dili%2C_East_Timor_%28312012049%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Motael_Church%2C_Dili%2C_East_Timor_%28312012049%29.jpg/340px-Motael_Church%2C_Dili%2C_East_Timor_%28312012049%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2077" data-file-height="2815"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Motael_Church,_Dili,_East_Timor_(312012049).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Church of <a href="/wiki/Motael_Church" title="Motael Church">Santo António de Motael</a>, Dili
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the 2015 census, 97.57% of the population is <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a>; 1.96% <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a>; 0.24% <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a>; 0.08% Traditional; 0.05% <a href="/wiki/Buddhist" class="mw-redirect" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a>; 0.02% <a href="/wiki/Hindu" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindu">Hindu</a>, and 0.08% other religions.<sup id="cite_ref-religion_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-religion-1">[1]</a></sup> A 2016 survey conducted by the <a href="/wiki/Demographic_and_Health_Survey" class="mw-redirect" title="Demographic and Health Survey">Demographic and Health Survey</a> programme showed that Catholics made up 98.3% of the population, Protestants 1.2%, and Muslims 0.3%.<sup id="cite_ref-DHS_2013_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DHS_2013-117">[117]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The number of churches has grown from 100 in 1974 to over 800 in 1994,<sup id="cite_ref-robinson_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-robinson-115">[115]</a></sup> with Church membership having grown considerably under <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesian</a> rule as <i><a href="/wiki/Pancasila_Indonesia" class="mw-redirect" title="Pancasila Indonesia">Pancasila</a></i>, Indonesia's state ideology, requires all citizens to believe in one <a href="/wiki/God" title="God">God</a> and does not recognise traditional beliefs. East Timorese <a href="/wiki/Animist" class="mw-redirect" title="Animist">animist</a> belief systems did not fit with <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Indonesia" title="Constitution of Indonesia">Indonesia's constitutional</a> <a href="/wiki/Monotheism" title="Monotheism">monotheism</a>, resulting in mass conversions to <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>. Portuguese clergy were replaced with Indonesian priests and <a href="/wiki/Latin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin language">Latin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> <a href="/wiki/Mass_in_the_Catholic_Church" title="Mass in the Catholic Church">mass</a> was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a> mass.<sup id="cite_ref-Taylor,_Jean_Gelman_2003,_p.381_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Taylor,_Jean_Gelman_2003,_p.381-118">[118]</a></sup> While just 20% of East Timorese called themselves Catholics at the time of the 1975 invasion, the figure surged to reach 95% by the end of the first decade after the invasion.<sup id="cite_ref-Taylor,_Jean_Gelman_2003,_p.381_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Taylor,_Jean_Gelman_2003,_p.381-118">[118]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> In rural areas, Roman Catholicism is <a href="/wiki/Religious_syncretism" title="Religious syncretism">syncretised</a> with local animist beliefs.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> With over 95% Catholic population, East Timor is currently the second <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_by_country" title="Catholic Church by country">most densely Catholic country</a> in the world, after the <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:8-Igreja_da_Imaculada_Concei%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Viqueque_2015-08-22.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/8-Igreja_da_Imaculada_Concei%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Viqueque_2015-08-22.jpg/220px-8-Igreja_da_Imaculada_Concei%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Viqueque_2015-08-22.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/8-Igreja_da_Imaculada_Concei%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Viqueque_2015-08-22.jpg/330px-8-Igreja_da_Imaculada_Concei%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Viqueque_2015-08-22.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/8-Igreja_da_Imaculada_Concei%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Viqueque_2015-08-22.jpg/440px-8-Igreja_da_Imaculada_Concei%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Viqueque_2015-08-22.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:8-Igreja_da_Imaculada_Concei%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Viqueque_2015-08-22.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i>Igreja da Imaculada Conceição</i> church, in <a href="/wiki/Viqueque_Municipality" title="Viqueque Municipality">Viqueque</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The number of <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestants</a> and <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslims</a> declined significantly after September 1999 because these groups were disproportionately represented among supporters of integration with <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> and among the Indonesian civil servants assigned to work in the province from other parts of Indonesia, many of whom left the country in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-report_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report-122">[122]</a></sup> There are also small Protestant and Muslim communities.<sup id="cite_ref-report_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report-122">[122]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_National_Armed_Forces" title="Indonesian National Armed Forces">Indonesian military forces</a> formerly stationed in the country included a significant number of Protestants, who played a major role in establishing Protestant churches in the territory.<sup id="cite_ref-report_122-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report-122">[122]</a></sup> Fewer than half of those congregations existed after September 1999, and many Protestants were among those who remained in <a href="/wiki/West_Timor" title="West Timor">West Timor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-report_122-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report-122">[122]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Assemblies_of_God" title="Assemblies of God">Assemblies of God</a> is the largest and most active of the Protestant denominations.<sup id="cite_ref-report_122-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report-122">[122]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>While the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_East_Timor" title="Constitution of East Timor">Constitution of East Timor</a> enshrines the principles of <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">freedom of religion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_church_and_state" title="Separation of church and state">separation of church and state</a> in Section 45 Comma 1, it also acknowledges "the participation of the Catholic Church in the process of national liberation" in its preamble (although this has no legal value).<sup id="cite_ref-constitution_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-123">[123]</a></sup> Upon independence, the country joined the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> to become the only two predominantly Roman Catholic states in Asia, although nearby parts of eastern Indonesia such as <a href="/wiki/West_Timor" title="West Timor">West Timor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flores" title="Flores">Flores</a> also have Roman Catholic majorities. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a> divides East Timor into <a href="/wiki/List_of_Roman_Catholic_dioceses_in_East_Timor" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Roman Catholic dioceses in East Timor">three dioceses</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_D%C3%ADli" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Díli">Diocese of Díli</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Baucau" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Baucau">Diocese of Baucau</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Maliana" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Maliana">Diocese of Maliana</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Timor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_East_Timor" title="Culture of East Timor">Culture of East Timor</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Lospalos_klein.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Lospalos_klein.jpg/170px-Lospalos_klein.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="248" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Lospalos_klein.jpg/255px-Lospalos_klein.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Lospalos_klein.jpg/340px-Lospalos_klein.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1188" data-file-height="1732"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Lospalos_klein.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Sacred house (<i>lee teinu</i>) in <a href="/wiki/Lospalos" title="Lospalos">Lospalos</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The culture of East Timor reflects numerous influences, including Portuguese, Roman Catholic and Indonesian, on Timor's <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">indigenous</a> <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Austronesian people">Austronesian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Melanesia" title="Melanesia">Melanesian</a> cultures. East Timorese culture is heavily influenced by Austronesian legends. For example, East Timorese <a href="/wiki/Creation_myth" title="Creation myth">creation myth</a> has it that an ageing <a href="/wiki/Crocodile" title="Crocodile">crocodile</a> transformed into the island of Timor as part of debt repayment to a young boy who had helped the crocodile when it was sick.<sup id="cite_ref-wiseamanda_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wiseamanda-125">[125]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> As a result, the island is shaped like a crocodile and the boy's descendants are the native East Timorese who inhabit it. The phrase "leaving the crocodile" refers to the pained exile of East Timorese from their island. East Timor is currently finalising its dossiers needed for nominations in the <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_List" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage List">World Heritage List</a>, <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_Intangible_Cultural_Heritage_Lists" title="UNESCO Intangible Cultural Heritage Lists">UNESCO Intangible Cultural Heritage Lists</a>, UNESCO <a href="/wiki/Creative_Cities_Network" title="Creative Cities Network">Creative Cities Network</a>, UNESCO <a href="/wiki/Global_Geoparks_Network" class="mw-redirect" title="Global Geoparks Network">Global Geoparks Network</a>, and UNESCO <a href="/wiki/Biosphere_Reserve" class="mw-redirect" title="Biosphere Reserve">Biosphere Reserve</a> Network. The country currently has one document in the UNESCO <a href="/wiki/Memory_of_the_World_Register" class="mw-redirect" title="Memory of the World Register">Memory of the World Register</a>, namely, <i>On the Birth of a Nation: Turning points</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts">Arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Timor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Timorese_Dancers.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Timorese_Dancers.jpg/170px-Timorese_Dancers.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Timorese_Dancers.jpg/255px-Timorese_Dancers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Timorese_Dancers.jpg/340px-Timorese_Dancers.jpg 2x" data-file-width="766" data-file-height="1024"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Timorese_Dancers.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Traditional Timorese dancers
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>There is a strong tradition of poetry in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> Prime Minister Xanana Gusmão, for example, is a distinguished poet, earning the moniker "poet warrior".<sup id="cite_ref-poetxan_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-poetxan-129">[129]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Architecturally, buildings are often Portuguese style along with the traditional totem houses of the eastern region. These are known as <i>uma lulik</i> ("sacred houses") in Tetum and <i>lee teinu</i> ("legged houses") in Fataluku.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Craftsmanship and the weaving of traditional scarves (<i>tais</i>) is also widespread.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>An extensive collection of Timorese audiovisual material is held at the <a href="/wiki/National_Film_and_Sound_Archive" title="National Film and Sound Archive">National Film and Sound Archive of Australia</a>. These holdings have been identified in a document titled The NFSA Timor-Leste Collection Profile, which features catalogue entries and essays for a total of 795 NFSA-held moving images, recorded sound and documentation works that have captured the history and culture of East Timor since the early 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> The NFSA is working with the East Timorese government to ensure that all of this material can be used and accessed by the people of that country.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema_and_TV_drama">Cinema and TV drama</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Timor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Cinema and TV drama">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In 2009 and 2010, East Timor was the setting for the Australian film <i><a href="/wiki/Balibo_(film)" title="Balibo (film)">Balibo</a></i> and the South Korean film <i><a href="/wiki/A_Barefoot_Dream" title="A Barefoot Dream">A Barefoot Dream</a></i>. In 2013, the first East Timorese feature film, <i><a href="/wiki/Beatriz%27s_War" title="Beatriz's War">Beatriz's War</a></i>, was released.<sup id="cite_ref-SMH_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SMH-132">[132]</a></sup> Two further feature-length films, <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abdul_%26_Jos%C3%A9&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Abdul &amp; José (page does not exist)">Abdul &amp; José</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Ema_Nudar_Umanu" title="Ema Nudar Umanu">Ema Nudar Umanu</a></i>, were respectively released on 30 July 2017 through the television network of <a href="/wiki/East_Timor_Broadcasting_Service" class="mw-redirect" title="East Timor Broadcasting Service">RTTL</a><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> and on 16 August 2018 at the <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_International_Film_Festival" title="Melbourne International Film Festival">Melbourne International Film Festival</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> In 2010, the first East Timorese TV drama, <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suku_Hali&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Suku Hali (page does not exist)">Suku Hali</a></i> was released.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Timor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_East_Timor" title="Cuisine of East Timor">cuisine of East Timor</a> consists of regional popular foods such as <a href="/wiki/Pork" title="Pork">pork</a>, fish, <a href="/wiki/Basil" title="Basil">basil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamarind" title="Tamarind">tamarind</a>, <a href="/wiki/Legumes" class="mw-redirect" title="Legumes">legumes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corn" class="mw-redirect" title="Corn">corn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Root_vegetables" class="mw-redirect" title="Root vegetables">root vegetables</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tropical_fruit" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical fruit">tropical fruit</a>. East Timorese cuisine has influences from <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asian_cuisine" class="mw-redirect" title="Southeast Asian cuisine">Southeast Asian cuisine</a> and from <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_cuisine" title="Portuguese cuisine">Portuguese dishes</a> from its colonisation by Portugal. Flavours and ingredients from other former Portuguese colonies can be found due to the centuries-old Portuguese presence on the island. Due to the East and West combination of East Timor's cuisine, it developed features related to <a href="/wiki/Filipino_cuisine" title="Filipino cuisine">Filipino cuisine</a>, which also experienced an east–west culinary combination. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Timor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_East_Timor" title="Sport in East Timor">Sport in East Timor</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:USMC-091018-M-9613D-009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/USMC-091018-M-9613D-009.jpg/220px-USMC-091018-M-9613D-009.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/USMC-091018-M-9613D-009.jpg/330px-USMC-091018-M-9613D-009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/USMC-091018-M-9613D-009.jpg/440px-USMC-091018-M-9613D-009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2528" data-file-height="1541"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:USMC-091018-M-9613D-009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>An East Timor versus U.S. service members soccer match at the <a href="/wiki/National_Stadium_(East_Timor)" title="National Stadium (East Timor)">National Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Dili" title="Dili">Dili</a> on 18 October 2009. The East Timor Secretary of Youth and Sports said the game was intended to promote peace and stability in the region. East Timor won 4–0.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Sports organisations joined by East Timor include the <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">International Olympic Committee</a> (IOC), the <a href="/wiki/International_Association_of_Athletics_Federations" class="mw-redirect" title="International Association of Athletics Federations">International Association of Athletics Federations</a> (IAAF), the International Badminton Federation (IBF), the <a href="/wiki/Union_Cycliste_Internationale" title="Union Cycliste Internationale">Union Cycliste Internationale</a>, the International Weightlifting Federation, the International Table Tennis Federation (ITTF), the International Basketball Federation (FIBA), and <a href="/wiki/East_Timor_national_football_team" class="mw-redirect" title="East Timor national football team">East Timor's national football team</a> joined <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a>. East Timorese athletes competed in the <a href="/wiki/2003_Southeast_Asian_Games" title="2003 Southeast Asian Games">2003 Southeast Asian Games</a> held 2003. In the 2003 ASEAN <a href="/wiki/Paralympics" class="mw-redirect" title="Paralympics">Paralympics</a> Games, East Timor won a bronze medal. In the <a href="/wiki/2004_Summer_Olympics" title="2004 Summer Olympics">Athens 2004 Olympic Games</a>, East Timorese athletes participated in athletics, weightlifting and boxing. East Timor <a href="/wiki/East_Timor_at_the_2005_Southeast_Asian_Games" title="East Timor at the 2005 Southeast Asian Games">won three medals</a> in <a href="/wiki/Arnis_at_the_2005_Southeast_Asian_Games" title="Arnis at the 2005 Southeast Asian Games">Arnis at the 2005 Southeast Asian Games</a>. East Timor competed in the <a href="/wiki/2006_Lusophony_Games" class="mw-redirect" title="2006 Lusophony Games">first</a> <a href="/wiki/Lusophony_Games" class="mw-redirect" title="Lusophony Games">Lusophony Games</a> and, in October 2008, the country earned its first international points in a <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> football match with a 2–2 draw against Cambodia.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> East Timor competed at the <a href="/wiki/2014_Winter_Olympics" title="2014 Winter Olympics">2014 Winter Olympics</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Thomas_Americo" title="Thomas Americo">Thomas Americo</a> was the first East Timorese fighter to fight for a world <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a> title. He was murdered in 1999, shortly before the Indonesian occupation of East Timor ended.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Timor&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFAdelman2011" class="citation book cs1">Adelman, Howard (28 June 2011). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=WRpHAAAAQBAJ&amp;q=east+timor+maubere&amp;pg=PA281"><i>No Return, No Refuge: Rites and Rights in Minority Repatriation</i></a>. Columbia University Press. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780231526906" title="Special:BookSources/9780231526906"><bdi>9780231526906</bdi></a> – via Google Books.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=No+Return%2C+No+Refuge%3A+Rites+and+Rights+in+Minority+Repatriation&amp;rft.pub=Columbia+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2011-06-28&amp;rft.isbn=9780231526906&amp;rft.aulast=Adelman&amp;rft.aufirst=Howard&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DWRpHAAAAQBAJ%26q%3Deast%2Btimor%2Bmaubere%26pg%3DPA281&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEast+Timor" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-Divided-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Divided_4-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Divided_4-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFShoesmith2003" class="citation journal cs1">Shoesmith, Dennis (March–April 2003). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://espace.cdu.edu.au/view/cdu:1248">"Timor-Leste: Divided Leadership in a Semi-Presidential System"</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Asian_Survey" title="Asian Survey">Asian Survey</a></i>. <b>43</b> (2): 231–252. <a href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1525%2Fas.2003.43.2.231">10.1525/as.2003.43.2.231</a>. <a href="/wiki/ISSN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISSN (identifier)">ISSN</a>&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.worldcat.org/issn/0004-4687">0004-4687</a>. <a href="/wiki/OCLC_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="OCLC (identifier)">OCLC</a>&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.worldcat.org/oclc/905451085">905451085</a>. <q>The semi-presidential system in the new state of Timor-Leste has institutionalized a political struggle between the president, Xanana Gusmão, and the prime minister, Mari Alkatiri. This has polarized political alliances and threatens the viability of the new state. This paper explains the ideological divisions and the history of rivalry between these two key political actors. The adoption of Marxism by Fretilin in 1977 led to Gusmão's repudiation of the party in the 1980s and his decision to remove Falintil, the guerrilla movement, from Fretilin control. The power struggle between the two leaders is then examined in the transition to independence. This includes an account of the politicization of the defense and police forces and attempts by Minister of Internal Administration Rogério Lobato to use disaffected Falintil veterans as a counterforce to the Gusmão loyalists in the army. The December 4, 2002, Dili riots are explained in the context of this political struggle.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Asian+Survey&amp;rft.atitle=Timor-Leste%3A+Divided+Leadership+in+a+Semi-Presidential+System&amp;rft.volume=43&amp;rft.issue=2&amp;rft.pages=231-252&amp;rft.date=2003-03%2F2003-04&amp;rft_id=info%3Aoclcnum%2F905451085&amp;rft.issn=0004-4687&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1525%2Fas.2003.43.2.231&amp;rft.aulast=Shoesmith&amp;rft.aufirst=Dennis&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fespace.cdu.edu.au%2Fview%2Fcdu%3A1248&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEast+Timor" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li>
